Hunan Fellow-Provincials Association Discusses the Case of Hunan Disaster Victims Killed by Villagers in Qingpu's Mao Dian

A Tragedy in Mao Dian: Villagers Kill 55 People with Weapons

Telegram to the Jiangsu Provincial Government Requesting an Investigation and Strict Punishment

Yesterday, the Hunan Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai convened an emergency meeting regarding the case of 55 disaster victims who fled famine from Xiangxiang County and were killed by villagers in the Mao Dian area of Qingpu County. Over 200 people attended, including Zhou Zhenlin, Ye Kaixin, Huang Yi'ou, Chen Heting, Shen Zurui, Li Wenhui, Zhou Gengxin, Ye Dingyuan, Ning Chunda, Li Wuyun, Zhang Chunsun, and Xiangxiang disaster victim representatives Li Shiying and Zhou Desheng. Zhou Zhenlin chaired the meeting, and Li Wuyun reported on the incident, stating that on the 15th of this month, the association received a report from Xiangxiang disaster victim representatives Yan Haiqing and Zhou Desheng. They stated that 148 disaster victims who fled famine from that county hired 15 boats on February 12th and arrived in the Mao Dian area. When they went ashore to beg for rice, the Mao Dian villagers not only refused to give them any but immediately beat gongs and gathered a crowd to attack them with weapons, throwing the bodies into the water. A total of 55 men, women, elderly people, and children were killed, and 29 were injured. They requested justice. On the morning of the 16th, the association sent Li Wenhui, Zhou Gengxin, and Zhang Chunsun to investigate and sent a letter to the Qingpu County Government Public Security Bureau, asking for their assistance. They returned to Shanghai on the 18th and reported that the number of disaster victims killed by Mao Dian villagers was confirmed. The county government sent personnel to supervise the undertakers in recovering the bodies, and 42 corpses were found, all with injuries of varying severity. Tragically, there were three corpses of children aged one year, two years, and eight months. The corpses were laid out waiting for coffins, a truly horrifying sight. They also questioned Shi Baoquan and Yang Gengquan, two local villagers aged around 70. According to them, at 9 AM on that day, representatives of the refugees went to Li Gengtang's house in the north of the village to ask for rice. He refused because Xiangxiang refugees had begged for 11 yuan in the village the previous day. So, he beat gongs and gathered the entire village to beat and drive them away, resulting in the deaths of many. They claimed they didn't know anything else. An investigation revealed that after the tragedy, all the villagers fled, leaving their houses and belongings intact. Armed soldiers from the county Public Security Bureau's security team have been sent to protect the area. County Magistrate Qian and Public Security Bureau Chief Huang have promised that the coffins will not be moved until the case is resolved. The fellow-provincials were outraged, saying that the disaster victims were refugees, what laws had they broken? Even if there was any disturbance, the 500-plus households of Mao Dian could have stopped it or reported it to the government, why did they resort to such brutal killing, resulting in 55 deaths and 29 injuries? The investigation revealed that all the houses and belongings were intact, indicating no disturbance. The entire village fled, showing their guilt. It was resolved that the legal aspects would be handled by lawyers Zhang Xingyan, Peng Ximin, and Chen Heting. Representatives will also be sent to Qingpu to negotiate seriously with the county government. On one hand, a telegram was sent to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, stating: "Chairman Chen of the Jiangsu Provincial Government and Director of the Civil Affairs Department, greetings. A case of men, women, elderly, and children fleeing famine from Xiangxiang reaching Mao Dian, Qingpu, being killed by the local villagers gathering and attacking them with weapons. These disaster victims suffered such a tragic fate, we are all human beings, how could they be so cruel? The incident is shockingly brutal and horrifying to hear. Our association has sent personnel to investigate and confirmed the details. The large Xiangxiang community in Shanghai is extremely angry. We are telegraphing to your office to dispatch personnel for a thorough investigation and strict legal punishment. More details will follow. From the Hunan Fellow-Provincials Association in Shanghai, Zhou Zhenlin, Ye Kaixin, Chen Jie, Huang Yi'ou, and over 200 others bow in reverence." Photos of the 42 corpses and the 29 injured men and women were taken and printed for distribution, disclosing the details of the tragedy, appealing to all provinces and sectors for justice for the disaster victims, and ensuring that tragedies like the Mao Dian incident do not happen again.

The Central Political Council Passes the Degree Conferral Law

Education Funding for Various Counties in Zhejiang Province Urgently Needs Relief

A Calamity the Likes of Which Has Not Been Seen Since the Founding of the Republic

Jiangshan County and Others Have the Most School Closures

(Hangzhou Correspondence) The education funding for various counties in Zhejiang Province has primarily come from the education surtax levied under the land tax. The second source is the rental income from school properties. However, since the severe drought and famine of the summer of the 23rd year, the land tax collection in various counties has been suspended, and the education surtax has been suspended accordingly. The rental income from school properties, which is proportional to the land tax, has also naturally stopped. Even in areas where the disaster affected less than 50%, allowing collection according to regulations, the collected amount is still very limited due to the bankruptcy of the rural economy. According to a reporter's investigation:

Education Funding for Various Counties

Statistics on Revenue Reductions Due to Disasters Showing Over 80% Reduction:

Haining, Dangyang, Lin'an, Xindeng, Haiyan, Tongxiang, Changxing, Nantian, Xiaoshan, Xianju, Pujiang, Jiande, Chun'an, Tonglu and fourteen other counties.

Over 70% Reduction:

Yuqian, Changhua, Wukang, Xiangshan, Shaoxing, Zhuji, Shangyu, Sheng County, Linhai, Wuyi, Longyou, Changshan, Shouchang and thirteen other counties.

Over 60% Reduction:

Hang County, Chongde, Pinghu, Wuxing, Anji, Xiaofeng, Cixi, Dinghai, Xinchang, Tiantai, Lanxi, Dongyang, Yongkang, Tangxi, Qu County, Jiangshan, Kaihua, Fenshui, Lishui, Qingtian, Jinyun, Songyang, Xuanping, Jingning and twenty-four other counties.

Over 50% Reduction:

Yuhang, Jiaxing, Jiashan, Deqing, Ningbo, Suian, Yunhe and seven other counties.

The severity of the disaster is truly shocking, unlike anything seen since the founding of the Republic. Consequently,

Schools Are Unable to Maintain Operations

and closures have been frequently reported. Jiangshan County has the highest number of closures with 86, followed by Dongyang County with 85. Tonglu and Shouchang counties both have 70. The rest range from 5-6 to 50-60 closures. There are also cases where schools have not officially closed, but are effectively empty and unsustainable, with classes long suspended. Therefore, the decrease in the number of students in various counties is also significant. Counties with a decrease of over 20 students include Yuhang, Dinghai, Xiaoshan, Shangyu, Sheng County, Pujiang, Jiande, and Tonglu. Counties with a decrease of over 1,000 students include Shaoxing, Xianju, Yongkang, Jiangshan, Fenshui, Lishui, and Qingtian. It is estimated that the dropout rate in Changhua, Haiyan, Wuxing, Lanxi, Dongyang, Longyou, and Suian has reached over 20%. In addition, there are many others where accurate data is unavailable but the actual decrease is significant. There are also many cases where teachers' salaries are in arrears for three to nine months. In view of the situation,

Education Funding Has Reached a Dead End

The education situation is unsustainable. Unless substantial financial aid is provided, education will be further disrupted, and the future is unimaginable. It is reported that the provincial government considers education to be fundamental to national development and is discussing ways to provide relief by issuing provincial public bonds to establish an education reserve fund for lending to various counties to maintain the precarious state of education. It is also reported that Director Xu of the Education Department believes that borrowing from public bonds is a temporary solution and that if a reliable method of guaranteeing local education funding is not established first, there will be instability every year. He emphasized the need for a fundamental solution and at the provincial government's weekly memorial service on the 11th of this month,

Proposed Five Measures

Hoping that the entire education sector in the province will mobilize to ensure their implementation so that local education can be effectively guaranteed in the future. The education bureaus and county party headquarters of various counties believe that planning for guaranteeing local education funding is urgently needed and consider these measures to be essential and easy to implement. They plan to unite all sectors on the ground to initiate and discuss implementation. The Education Department is concerned that the measures in various regions will be too diverse and that the methods for managing and safeguarding education funds may not be entirely adequate. It is drafting an outline for increasing and reorganizing education funding for various counties and cities to provide guidance.

The Ministry of Education Plans to Develop Border Education

Editing Elementary School Textbooks Suitable for Various Ethnic Groups

Establishing Normal Schools to Cultivate Teachers with Pure Ideologies

The Ministry of Education believes that education in China's border regions is extremely backward due to the lack of funds, which prevents development. It has requested the Executive Yuan to allocate 350,000 yuan from the Boxer Indemnity in the next fiscal year to subsidize education funding in border provinces and regions so that border education can gradually develop. A reporter spoke with officials from the Ministry of Education yesterday about the department's recent investigations into the state of education in the border provinces and the planned development measures, as follows:

Current Status of Border Education

Investigations show that Suiyuan, Chahar, Qinghai, Ningxia, Xikang, and Yunnan are important border areas of China. The local governments in these areas either lack foresight or are limited by financial and human resources and have greatly neglected education. Often, there are no government-established schools or schools that use Chinese textbooks for instruction in hundreds or thousands of miles or dozens of counties. With the national crisis so severe, this is a major danger signal. The situation of the mixed population of Mongol, Hui, Tibetan, and Miao peoples in the border provinces and their current educational state are described as follows: Apart from those residing in Outer Mongolia and the three northeastern provinces, the largest Mongol populations are in Suiyuan and Chahar provinces. Since the Qing dynasty opened the border between Han and Mongol areas in the late Qing dynasty, some of the natives have been assimilated by the Han people and are proficient in Chinese. However, this is only true for a small number of intellectuals, and most Mongols still prioritize the Mongol language. According to 1930 statistics, there are only over 800 elementary schools in the two provinces of Chahar and Suiyuan, and most of them are for children of Han people. Very few Mongolians attend. Xinjiang, Qinghai, and Ningxia are areas where Hui people live in concentrated communities, especially Xinjiang. The general population of Xinjiang is estimated at 2.5 million, Qinghai at approximately 3 million, and Ningxia at approximately 450,000, most of whom are Hui. According to 1930 statistics, there are only 5-6,000 elementary school students in school, and Hui children are still a minority. The low level of their culture and knowledge is self-evident. Recently, Russians have taken the opportunity to penetrate the region and entice the youth of the province to study in their country, which is worrying. Xikang is inhabited by Tibetans. Since the British invasion of Tibet, China's political influence in Kang has been hanging by a thread. If we do not pay attention to education and enlighten the people, the future is unimaginable. Currently, there are only over 40 elementary schools, and the number of Tibetan people attending school and receiving education is still small. In Yunnan, the Han population accounts for only about one-third of the total population of the province. A portion of the Mongolian people and the majority of the Miao people live in mixed communities with indigenous ethnic groups, and their knowledge is very rudimentary. According to reports from the Yunnan Provincial Education Department, about 30 counties in the province still do not have government-established schools. Foreign missionaries have recently been gradually increasing their influence in these areas. Recently, French missionaries have established normal schools and set up elementary schools for the Miao people, teaching them with a clear purpose. Previously, the Education Department of the province drafted measures to implement border education in order to remedy the situation, but they have not been able to proceed due to limited funding and a lack of textbooks for language instruction. Given the above situation, the situation in the border regions is deteriorating daily. To strengthen our borders, we must promote education and foster a sense of unity and resistance to invasion. However, the various ethnic groups in the border regions live in mixed communities. Except for a few who have been assimilated by the Han people, most of the people have different languages and writing systems. Without teaching tools, plans cannot be implemented. This has been a shared pain for border education administrative bodies throughout history. Therefore, the fundamental issue should be to pay attention to the editing of special textbooks for various ethnic groups and the establishment of elementary school teachers. The following measures are proposed:

Development Plan

(A) Editing elementary school textbooks suitable for various ethnic groups (1) Key points: The content should pay attention to the inherent characteristics of the ethnic groups, instill scientific knowledge, and include materials on national humiliation and historical figures who defended the country to enlighten knowledge and foster patriotism. (2) Method: First compile three types of textbooks: National Language, Civics, and General Knowledge (including history, geography, and natural sciences). All three should be based on the National Language with annotations in Mongolian, Hui, and Miao languages. (B) Establishing elementary schools extensively (1) Key points: Schools should be established first in the most culturally backward areas of the border regions to train children in basic education and use the schools as centers to instill common sense and patriotic ideas in the general population. (2) Method: Twelve Mongolian elementary schools should be established first, four in the twelve banners of Chahar Province, three in the ten banners of Xilin Gol League, two in the six banners of Ulanqab League, two in the seven banners of Yeke Joo League, one in Alxa Special Banner, and one in Ejina Special Banner. Nine Hui elementary schools should be established first, four in the twenty-nine Mongolian banners of Qinghai, one in the twenty-three Mongolian banners of Xinjiang, and four in the Hui areas of Xinjiang. Four Tibetan elementary schools should be established in Xikang, and ten Miao elementary schools should be established first in Yunnan. (C) Establishing normal schools (1) Key points: Teacher training is the basis of all facilities. Without qualified personnel, it will be difficult to achieve good results. Normal schools should be established in suitable locations in various border areas to recruit outstanding Han and ethnic minority youth, provide them with rigorous training, and cultivate persistent, pure-thinking teachers. (2) Method: Two Mongolian normal schools should be established first, one in Zhangjiakou and one in Guihua. Two Hui normal schools should be established first, one in Xining and one in Dihua. One Tibetan normal school should be established first in Kangding. Five schools should be established in Yunnan, one each in Deqin (i.e., Dunzi), Zhenkang, Cheli, Jinsha River, and Qiuta.

The Ministry of Education Orders Schools to Enlighten the Public with Scientific Knowledge

(Nanjing, 20th) The Ministry of Education, according to the China Association for the Advancement of Science, states that if the lives of the people are not scientific and production is not improved, the general public will lack the ability to participate in resolving the national crisis and revitalizing the nation. At this time of national difficulty, school staff and students should use their spare time to popularize scientific knowledge to the public so that schools and society are closely linked and people's livelihoods can be improved. As the spring semester begins, an order is issued to all levels of schools across the country to hold at least one public science lecture each month. Primary and secondary schools must also organize science lecture competitions each semester and welcome the general public to attend, in order to improve public scientific knowledge. A special order is issued to universities and colleges and transmitted to all levels of affiliated schools for compliance.

International Rural Film Competition Hosted by the International Educational Cinematographic Institute

To be held in Brussels in July

China Invited to Participate

A grand international exhibition will be held in Brussels this year. The Belgian Committee for the Improvement of Rural Life, with the support of the International Educational Cinematographic Institute, the International Committee for the Improvement of Rural Life, and the cooperation of family education and rural associations, will hold a rural film competition. The Chinese Educational Film Association has received formal notification and hopes that the Chinese film industry will participate. The details are as follows:

(1) "Motivation": Film has become a trend in various countries around the world. Today, it has become a universal world language for humanity, at least as a powerful tool for promoting new ideals and education. Its immense value in agriculture is undeniable, from family life to construction, from youth education to fieldwork. It is used to promote the application of technology in rural areas and fieldwork and life, and to promote the value of rural life in cities. It is a tool for rural education and can also be used to promote its products. To encourage the production of films most suitable for rural areas, an international rural film competition has been organized.

(2) "Scope of Competition": The competition will reward and widely promote the films that are most successful in addressing the following three topics: A. Films that can best promote the improvement of farms, such as rural construction and architecture, including rural landscapes. B. Films that can best promote the rationalization of rural family management. C. Films that promote the progress of rural education, with special attention to the development of children's character.

(3) "Prizes": The best film in each category will be awarded a Special Prize Certificate. The second-place film will be awarded an Honorary Certificate. The remaining three films of value will be awarded medals. In addition, 4,000 francs will be given to the jury to purchase meaningful films.

(4) "Date": July 23-27 this year. Films participating in the competition will be screened by the organizing committee at the International Exhibition venue.

(5) "Registration": Each country can submit a maximum of two films for competition. It is best for each country to hold domestic preliminary competitions to decide the entries. The registration fee is 100 francs and should be submitted before May 1st.

(6) "Judges": Judging will focus on internationality, with one official representative and one alternate representative from each participating country forming the jury.

The Belgian Committee for the Improvement of Rural Life believes that the future of rural films is extremely promising. At this initial stage, it will take advantage of the competition to organize a temporary exhibition. All materials related to the scope of rural films can be sent for exhibition. Rural areas are currently the most important economic and social issue. Participation in this international competition is an excellent opportunity to understand the rural life of various countries and exchange films, and to encourage development in this direction. It has also been resolved to request central guidance in producing two rural life films to participate in the competition.

Shen Bao Women's Tutorial School Makes Great Progress

The Shen Bao Women's Tutorial School, located at No. 75 Xieqiao Lane, Jing'an Temple Road in this city, is established for older, uneducated women. The elementary level teaches basic knowledge such as Chinese, English, mathematics, and general knowledge. The advanced level is divided into two subjects: Home Affairs and Vocational Skills. In addition to basic knowledge, the Home Affairs subject adds courses such as sewing, embroidery, and abacus. The Vocational Skills subject adds courses such as bookkeeping, typing, shorthand, and service knowledge. There are morning and afternoon classes, which can be selected according to the convenience of the students' time. Subjects can also be selected for study as needed. It is reported that this semester has already started on the 11th. In addition to all the courses offered last year, new teaching materials have been added, and a new course in bank bookkeeping has been added for women aspiring to be bankers. More attention is paid to extracurricular activities, such as national music and publications. Recently, many people have been signing up and registering.

Special Publication

Pan Gongzhan's Speech on Shanghai's School Education (3)

I believe that China's education, since the rise of schools after the Sino-Japanese War of 1894, has only been around for forty years. And in these forty years of education, only 2.4 percent of the population is enrolled in schools, which is truly absurd. Do we still want to run education in the same way as before? The previous method of running schools was a superficial one. When others had something, we wanted to learn it too. When others had elementary schools, we wanted to have elementary schools too. When others had kindergartens, we wanted to have kindergartens too. When others had middle schools, we wanted to have middle schools too. When others had universities, we wanted to have universities too. Even when others had diploma mills, we wanted to have diploma mills too. It was as if not having what others had was a disgrace, and we didn't even bother to understand what was inside each level of school. Therefore, we fundamentally neglected elementary education, which is a major flaw. Therefore, our future education policy, not just in Shanghai but throughout the country, should pay attention to the issue of "elementary education." This is a major issue for China's "survival," not a child's play. It's not that I'm exaggerating the seriousness of education because I'm in charge of Shanghai's education administration. Even in the business community, the children of those in the business community also need to be educated, and "elementary education" is indeed a basic education that everyone must go through. No matter what field, it must be emphasized.

Some people think that there are already a lot of students now. If we take the ratio, if one out of twenty elementary school students in our country can go to middle school, then we should have 500,000 middle school students now. If one out of ten middle school students can go to university, then we should have 50,000 university students in our country. In the past, those who ran education in our country and a group of students thought that going to school was only to prepare for becoming an official, as if it were still the same as in the imperial examination era. In the past, the "provincial examination" was held once every three years. Usually, a province only selected a hundred or so people, and at most two hundred or so. Some culturally backward provinces didn't even select a hundred people. But now there are about 11 million elementary school students in the country, accounting for 236 out of every 10,000 people in the country. There are about 520,000 middle school students, accounting for 11 out of every 10,000 people in the country. There are more than 40,000 university and vocational school students, accounting for 1 out of every 10,000 people in the country. Perhaps it feels like this number is a lot. But you should know that the purpose of running education is not for students to prepare to become officials in the future. If we run education with this attitude, then we should just close many schools. When the imperial examination was abolished and schools were established at the end of the Qing Dynasty, I heard people say that graduating from higher elementary school was like having the qualifications of a "bachelor" in the Qing Dynasty. Graduating from middle school was probably equivalent to a "recommended scholar" in the Qing Dynasty. Graduating from university was like a "Hanlin scholar" in the Qing Dynasty. Students who returned from studying abroad were considered "foreign Hanlin scholars." Some people made such comparisons, isn't it just like the imperial examination? What I'm saying is not a joke. Even now, there are still such similar situations. Although the titles of "bachelor," "recommended scholar," and "Hanlin scholar" are gone, aren't there still "bachelor's" degrees after graduating from university? And further up, aren't there titles like "master's" and "doctor's" degrees for students who have studied abroad? Although middle school graduates don't have any titles, I have heard that there are still some provinces where, after their children graduate from middle school, the clansmen open the ancestral hall, ask them to worship their ancestors, and even issue announcements. People who run and receive education like this still have such feudal thoughts now. If we turn it around and say that education is to teach people to survive, to teach people to have knowledge, to teach people to have skills, to teach people to have the ability to live, who doesn't want these knowledge, skills, and ability to seek a living and survive? Therefore, everyone should be educated, at least until they have completed "elementary education." Therefore, "elementary education" is also called "compulsory education." There are two aspects to the explanation of "compulsory education": (1) If children reach the appropriate school age and their parents don't send them to elementary school, then the government will force them to go to elementary school, and the parents will be punished. Why? This "elementary education" must be received by everyone, as if it is an obligation. (2) We can also say that "compulsory education" is the obligation of the state. The state should establish more elementary schools so that these children who have reached school age have the right to enjoy this education for free. In short, no matter how you say it, "compulsory education" is a fundamental education. But what is the situation of "compulsory education" in our country now? To this day, "elementary education" only accounts for 2.4 percent of the total population. However, according to the brief report just now, everyone can recognize the trend of Shanghai's education. Although the number of elementary school students is still far from the goal of at least 340,000, the increase in the number of elementary school students in recent years is a relatively gratifying phenomenon. We hope that this phenomenon will continue to develop, and we hope that the strength of all students' parents and all citizens will be concentrated to cooperate with the government and develop in this direction. Whether it is public or private, we will do our best to help. As long as we have a bit of strength, we will do our best. In this way, we will have fulfilled a considerable responsibility to the country, to society, and to this city. Because our strength is very weak at this time, we can only first work hard on running "elementary education." I hope everyone can work together to get this road right first, and then talk about other things. Only by concentrating our efforts on one point can we see results. (To be continued)

Requirements for Referees in the Citywide Elementary School Shuttlecock Kicking Competition

There are also regulations for posture standards

The Shanghai Education Bureau has scheduled the citywide elementary school shuttlecock kicking competition to be held in districts starting at 9:30 AM on February 23rd. The competition rules have been announced by the bureau. The following are the requirements for referees during the competition:

(1) All referees must arrive at the shuttlecock kicking competition location before 9:30 AM on February 23rd. (2) Five minutes before the start of the competition, draw lots in groups to determine the order of the competitors. There is no need to hold a ceremony. (3) Referees should pay attention to the actual competition situation in each district at any time. After the competition, the referee report form should be sent to the Experiment Division of the Third Section by the morning of February 25th for sorting. (4) The referee report form will be issued to each referee by the Third Section. Be sure to bring the form to the venue for application. (5) Referee scoring: (1) Shuttlecock production, maximum 10 points; (2) Posture, maximum 30 points; (3) Number of kicks, maximum 60 points. (6) The top three students in each group in each district will be determined by the top three with the highest total score in each group. The results will be reported to the public by the referees of each district on the same day. (7) In principle, two or three referees will judge one group. If there are many competitors, the referees may simultaneously serve as referees for various groups. (8) The best posture is to keep the spine straight, the pelvis moving freely, and the whole body is exceptionally lively without hindering breathing and blood circulation. (9) Each school is free to choose representatives of either gender and the shoes and boots worn by the representatives. (10) If any representative is found to have bought a name or cheated, the referee may cancel their qualification for the competition. If it is discovered afterwards, it should be reported to the Director for verification and handling.

Business News

Finance

Fuchang Closes Long Positions, Gold Price Breaks 900 Yuan

Many Seize the Opportunity to Buy Low

Repeated Rallies Result in a 5 Yuan Drop

The gold market has been declining steadily for days, with no sign of recovery. Long positions are being closed one after another. Unexpectedly, even Fuchang, the last remaining major long player, also closed its long positions yesterday, causing the price to break the 900 yuan barrier repeatedly. However, because the Central Bank continued to support the shilling, there were still many who stepped in to buy long. There were several rallies in between, but confidence remained weak, and the upward momentum was only temporary. Some parties aggressively bought at low prices, eventually leading to a stalemate. The morning started with overseas silver markets rising across the board, exchange rates slightly contracting, and London spot gold rising by three and a half pence. Sentiment continued to trend downward. Off-exchange trading opened lower at 0.034 yuan, and large traders immediately sold, briefly falling to one yuan. Short covering then surged, pushing the price back up to 0.034 yuan. When the Central Bank's exchange rates were announced, both the British and American rates had increased, while the customs gold unit fell by one cent, showing slight weakness. The morning opened with a low, which then turned higher. However, the loose domestic market brought a flood of sellers taking advantage of the high prices, leading to an oversupply. Despite some support at the lows, the price ultimately fell due to overwhelming selling pressure. Retail investors were eager for lower prices, and the 900 yuan barrier was finally broken. Anticipating that the Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation (HSBC) would not move its rates, the price rebounded. The Central Bank's support of the shilling boosted morale and triggered a rally. However, banks quickly seized the opportunity to sell, and large short players exerted pressure, loosening the exchange rate. Hedgers also came in to sell, thwarting the rally and pushing the price gradually downward, breaking the 900 yuan barrier again. Yifeng, Yongyuanmao, Yongda, Decheng, and other major players vigorously bought bullion, providing support. The Central Bank continued to support the shilling, making a recovery easier, but the rally was only temporary. After reaching a high, the supply of gold increased significantly, causing the price to fluctuate widely. Government Bonds Rise Alone

According to a report from Xinfeng Foreign Firm, yesterday (19th), the New York stock market showed a downward trend due to a lack of demand. Oil Market

Foreign Firms' Supply of Tung Oil Uninterrupted

Domestic Sales Exceptionally Sluggish

Following the settlement of accounts for tung oil, foreign firms in Hankou briefly experienced a lull, potentially easing market conditions. However, the arrival of goods has not significantly increased, and previously sold futures contracts are continuously reaching maturity, keeping prices stable. Only March futures experienced a slight dip to 29.8 yuan, while spot oil remained at 30 yuan, with little available. Recently, the situation in Hankou has remained strong. Although foreign firms are only handling dozens of tons, prices have already increased to 30.03 yuan net, indicating that prices cannot fall further. It is reported that prices for tung oil in Xiangtong, Hankou, are around 25 yuan, and it is said that supplies are not increasing. Traders are hesitant to sell to foreign firms, suggesting that tung oil from Hankou may not enter customs at 30 yuan after all. As for transactions by foreign firms in this port, exports have reached tens of thousands of tons annually in recent years. The sole source is Zhejiang, although some supplies from southern Anhui are transported through Zhejiang, the overall quantity is small. Therefore, exporters in Shanghai dare not sell too much. Although transactions of two to three hundred tons were seen last winter, this was at the beginning of the season. Normally, such large transactions would be unlikely, as Zhejiang's production is insufficient to meet Shanghai's foreign sales. Even if production increases in the coming years, demand is also increasing daily. Recently, the market price in Hangzhou is over 31 yuan per dan, while foreign firms offer only a little over 32 yuan, making foreign trade difficult to initiate. Domestic sales are particularly slow this spring. The drought in Zhejiang, an area of disaster, means no one is interested, as expected. Sales in Jiangsu are also less strong than in previous years, so the decline in domestic sales, compared to previous years, is a stark contrast.

Random Notes

Snippets

— (Shen Shou Ruo)

The government has explicitly banned the old practice of calling officials "Master," but people still do so secretly. One official secretly took a concubine. Upon entering the house, the concubine was instructed to kowtow to the first wife, making it difficult for the first wife to object. However, the concubine was, of course, very reluctant and, upon entering the room, began to fuss and complain to the official. Fortunately, the official had a sudden inspiration and kowtowed to the concubine as well, which appeased her anger. It is said that this is one of the secrets to taking a concubine, called "balancing the accounts."

My friend, Mr. Sun Pinglv, is friends with Deng Fenweng, the main organizer of the Crying Society. When he returned during the winter vacation, he happened to mention Deng's recent situation. According to him, he encountered Deng Fenweng previously, and during their conversation, Deng planned to name his study Pan Studio, his poetry collection Donkey Collection, and his hall Little Leisure Hall. When asked about the meaning behind these names, he said that old novels often contain the phrase "Pan, Donkey, Deng, Little, Leisure." His surname is Deng, which has a connection to four characters in this phrase. Therefore, he jokingly used it to name his residence and poetry collection. This old man's actions can be described as amusing.

Lantern Market in Taixian County

— Yun Sun

Taixian County used to be called a prefecture. It was downgraded to a county after the founding of the Republic. In the era of the imperial examinations, there was a distinction between prefecture exams and county exams. Taizhou at that time could be called the second-best in Yangzhou. Taixian County does not have many kinds of products, but "Taizhou Lanterns" and "Small Stone Mill Sesame Oil" are refined products that enjoy a good reputation in the Jiangnan region! Therefore, even today, the lantern market is still the best in the eight counties. The lanterns in Shanghai's amusement parks are mostly crystallizations of craftsmanship. However, the "elegant but not extravagant" gauze lanterns are still first-class products of Taizhou. According to legend, there used to be a "gauze lantern" that, when lit, did not cast a shadow. Who knows what broke the feng shui? This intangible relic has only been transformed into a topic of conversation after tea and wine. The Spring Lantern Festival, from the thirteenth to the eighteenth day of the first lunar month, is when many hundreds of craftsmen make a living. They first construct the framework of the lantern and then engage in pasting and mounting work at the end of the year. It goes on the market on the fifth day and ends on the thirteenth. Slope Street, from Zhongshan Gate to Dangjun Building, is crowded every day, forming a line of lanterns, a universe of lanterns. Flying birds and walking animals are for children to play with, while "crowns," "belts," "boats," and "pomegranates" are for good luck. A Ming Dynasty prime minister's hat, a jade belt, a painted boat, and a pomegranate make up a set of lanterns filled with feudal flavor. Literary people and scholars buy two-colored wall lamps, also known as revolving lanterns. Kongming playing the "Empty City Stratagem" and Zhao Zilong fighting at "Changban Slope" are all taken from the Romance of the Three Kingdoms. Uncles and aunts buy lanterns for their nephews, and parents buy lanterns for their newly married daughters. These are unbreakable customs. There is a saying that "you can't raise a servant girl," probably because people dislike these trivial etiquettes. Visitors who have seen the screen lanterns at Guandi Temple and Yue Tomb then turn to the lantern market to buy a few sets of lanterns. The lantern market ends after the "old face lanterns" are sold on the thirteenth day. Under the moonlight of early spring, silver is spread across the earth, and children throughout the city light all kinds of lanterns, forming a transformed art exhibition of lantern craftsmen.

Sketch of a Gambling Den

— Yang Yusheng

Changfa Tea Garden is where "yin energy" concentrates in our countryside. Every Lunar New Year, it is customary to have a lively celebration!

In the southeast corner of the tea garden, a pile of human bodies stacked like Arhats. The noisy voices made it impossible to distinguish what they were arguing about!

"Shrink your hand... Shrink... Your hand!" Zhang Dagou, sitting to the right of the dark-skinned man from Jiangbei known as Lao Si, shouted loudly. A melon-rind cap was tilted on one-fifth of his forehead, truly giving him the air of hair standing on end in anger!

Jiangbei Lao Si raised the two dice high and threw them onto the table on the last syllable of Zhang Dagou's shout "Catch... Eat"! Zhang Dagou followed with a shout of "Nine"! What followed was a powerful "Sweep the pot"! In these few seconds, the tense atmosphere locked the mouths of all the gamblers, and the air was strangely silent!

"Ah! Jiangbei Lao Si has another dud ten!" The gamblers' mouths were freed! Laughing! Shouting! Their hands were busy scooping up the silver dollars being paid out!

"Waiter... Wring out a towel!" Jiangbei Lao Si shouted anxiously, his face dark and red, unspeakably ugly.

Zhang Dagou, puffing out his cheeks, stood up abruptly, grabbed the melon-rind cap and slammed it on the table, shouting a string of requests to the waiter to burn paper ingots! To ward off ghosts!

Then, a blaze of fire rose in front of the Changfa Tea Garden, and the smiling faces of the gamblers gradually disappeared in the firelight!

Old Goods Peddler

— Long Dan

According to a person who carries an old goods load, there are three thousand old goods loads in Shanghai. I don't know if this number is accurate, because no one has officially investigated it. However, I feel that their number is indeed very large. Whether it is sunny or cloudy, you can find their traces in the streets and alleys.

Most of the people who do this business are from Jiangbei. They carry two balanced bamboo baskets to buy old goods everywhere, and then carry the gathered goods to the old goods tea party for sale, or carry them to the market (meaning selling to colleagues).

"Birds of a feather flock together." The old goods peddlers also have gatherings (they call them tea parties). In Zhabei alone, there are two old goods tea parties: in the morning, they are all on Xin Jia Road, and in the afternoon, they are all on Da Tong Road. There, the items they display are very rich. Whether it is ancient and modern calligraphy and painting, seasonal clothes, household utensils, and other miscellaneous items, they are always all available. And they are also very accommodating with the price. Often, after bargaining for three to five yuan, they will make a deal with you after a few cents.

They also use a secret language when trading with colleagues. Usually, they use "口, 人, 工, 比, 才; 爲, 春, 本, 金, 石," (transliteration) to represent "一, 二, 三, 四, 五, 六, 七, 八, 九, 十." Ten characters. For example, to say one yuan, they say "口字洋錢"; three jiao is called "工角", five hundred cash is called "才百錢", and others are not listed in detail.

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Nine: Failure to Return Home Due to Inept Flattery and Deceptive Exaggeration

The Hu family, supporting the wall, walked to the front room of Cheng Zhi. Besides the host, there was also a man and a woman. The man was wearing short clothes and had his chest open. The Hu family understood that this was called Western clothes. The woman was hard to explain. Her face was also covered with rouge and powder. Her hair was puffed up, with many curls piled high on her head, somewhat like the Western women on cigarette cards. She wore a green long dress that dragged along her heels. Under the light, it glittered with gold. She had never seen such a thing in her life. Could it be the Dharma robe bestowed by the Goddess of Mercy in the drum songs? Moreover, her appearance was even stranger. Such a long dress, but the sleeves were so short, almost short to the armpits. As soon as the Hu family stepped into the door, supporting the wall, she took in the woman completely. Although Yueying was a little more sensible, she didn't know the rules that servants should observe when meeting their master. So after she entered the room, she only called out "Master Cheng" to Cheng Zhiqian, and then said "We are here." The man was fine, but the woman, because the Hu family was staring at her, was already full of anger. She first made a sound of disapproval, turned her head and said to Zhiqian: "Mr. Cheng, are you introducing this kind of person to work for me? This woman's dead eyes stared at me without blinking, how annoying, three parts not like a person, seven parts like a ghost, not having any manners when seeing people, and supporting the wall without letting go." The man smiled and said: "How can she not support the wall? Her three-inch golden lotuses can't stand up." The woman said, her eyes already shooting at Yueying, sniffing and nodding: "This child, if bought to be a maid, might be trained after two or three months. What's the use of this small-footed woman?" The woman was standing, but she crossed her legs while speaking, looking very imposing. The Hu family could see through her. However, seven or eight out of ten of her words were spoken with a southern accent, and she didn't understand them very well. (One Three Eight)

Records of Imperial Fragrance飘渺

— Original by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shou Ou

Fortunately, she immediately expressed her approval upon hearing it, which greatly calmed my mind. Moreover, as she walked towards the place where the opera was being performed, she enthusiastically told me the plot of the play "Si Lang Visits His Mother" in detail. Actually, since I knew about this play, how could I not know the plot? However, the Empress Dowager absolutely didn't care. She always liked to act like an old woman, treating every little detail as a new piece of knowledge, a new invention, and telling it to others in a solemn manner. And the listeners, intimidated by her accumulated power, even if they really didn't want to listen in their hearts, couldn't help but pretend to be very interested and listen attentively. If they didn't do this, or couldn't help but laugh, it would be a great breach of etiquette! So we were all used to this kind of forced listening and would no longer annoy her.

But in all fairness, although she seemed to have too much interest in telling stories, often forcing people to listen, she was indeed talented. A very ordinary story, after she told it, would be much more moving than the original. Whether it was the first, second, or even the fifth or sixth time she repeated the story, it would never lack any excitement, so sometimes we did listen with great interest.

Before long, we arrived in front of the stage. The Empress Dowager sat down on the throne placed in the center, and we all stood on both sides behind her, as usual. I looked up at the stage and couldn't help but admire the abilities of the eunuchs. They had managed to clean up this dilapidated stage in a very short time and had tried their best to imitate the style of the one in the Summer Palace, almost imitating it by three or four points. Small Recipe

New Year's Desserts

— Zhu 

During the Lunar New Year, every household, due to the visits of relatives and friends, some refined families prepared various soups in addition to desserts, such as "Date Lotus Seed Soup" and "Lotus Seed Soup," to entertain guests. Small households also prepared a few kinds of desserts to satisfy guests' hunger. Because of social customs, it is impossible not to eat some food when visiting someone's home for the first time during the New Year. Thus, desserts have become an essential food for every household.

Suzhou families prepare approximately the following types of desserts:

Cake Suzhou people love to seek good fortune. Because the pronunciation of "cake" contains the auspicious meanings of "happy and prosperous" and "prosperity and good fortune," cake becomes the main item among New Year's desserts. There are also several kinds of cake, such as yellow and white New Year cake. Cut into pieces, it can be used to make cake soup. Cut into slices, it can be used to stir-fry New Year cake. Lard cake also comes in several flavors, such as rose, mint, jujube paste, and white sugar. Cut into thin slices, steamed, boiled, or stir-fried, it is sweet and very flavorful. Song cake is also very delicious. There is also a kind of "Ningbo New Year Cake," white strips, cut into small pieces. It can be used to cook soup with dried shrimp and winter bamboo shoots, and it can also be stir-fried with lard and shredded meat. It is also a very good savory dessert.

Steamed Bun Because of the saying "Prosperous Steamed Bun," steamed buns have become a dessert representing the auspicious meaning of prosperity. Among New Year's desserts, it is absolutely indispensable. This kind of steamed bun uses unleavened flour. The skin is thin, the meat is large and juicy, and the taste is very delicious. When people eat it, some steam it and some deep-fry it, depending on the guest's preference.

Spring Roll This is a homemade dessert. Stir-fry winter bamboo shoots or shepherd's purse with shredded meat, and then take the spring roll skins bought from the market (which are round flour pancakes), peel them off one by one, and wrap the stir-fried winter bamboo shoots and shredded meat or shepherd's purse and shredded meat inside, rolling them into small rolls like "knot-shaped bean curd sheets." When eating, they must be deep-fried in oil. Crispy and delicious, they have a special flavor.

Rice Dumpling This is also homemade, with several types such as jujube, salted meat, and bean paste. Jujube rice dumplings have a few jujubes added to the white rice. For salted meat rice dumplings, the fresh meat is also braised thoroughly in soy sauce, and then the washed rice is also mixed with soy sauce and wrapped together. This kind of rice dumpling must be wrapped loosely and cooked thoroughly, so that it melts in the mouth when eaten and has a delicious taste. Bean paste rice dumplings are wrapped with rice and bean paste and also require being cooked loosely and soft as the main condition.

Dumpling This is the most elaborate dessert of Suzhou families. Its fillings are divided into as many as seven or eight kinds, such as meat, lard bean paste, lard radish shreds, thorny paste, and so on. When making dumplings, first make all kinds of fillings, then knead the rice flour, wrap the dumplings and make them into dumplings, and then put them in a steamer to cook. When eating, some re-steam them, and some cook them in soup like Tangyuan.

A Word of Contribution

The Education Community and the "Student National Products Year"

— Xuan Wan

To trace the path of national products this year from the five characters "Student National Products Year," then, undeniably, in this year, the education community of our country should first shoulder the mission of promoting national products and move forward with large strides on the path of "national products education."

The trade deficit of China in recent years and the increasing decline of the national economy have long been known to people with insight. They know that it will not be successful unless we revitalize industry and drive out foreign goods. However, what about our education community, which is known as the advanced in knowledge? Has it made considerable efforts in the past to maintain domestic products? I remember Mr. Tai Shuangqiu once said: "Our country's schools are all agencies for selling foreign goods, and our country's teachers and students are all salesmen of foreign goods." These two sentences are aimed at the reality of our country's education community, and there is no falsehood. We know that from the buildings in the schools to the equipment and materials used, most of them are foreign goods, so that students in the education era! Some cannot produce, but have already consumed a lot of foreign goods. Assuming that the total number of students in the country is one million, then the average person consumes two yuan of imported goods per year, which is a staggering 20 million yuan. What responsibility does it have for contributing to the surge in the trade deficit and the bankruptcy of the national economy?

Although, remembering the past and striving for the future, if our education community can catch up quickly, the past shame can still be washed away. I dare to write down the two things that I hope everyone will earnestly implement below:

First, to make students abandon foreign goods and love domestic products, our education community should first set an example by doing it ourselves. We should usually wear uniforms made of domestic materials, and all conversations, actions, and objects used must be based on the principle of promoting domestic products. Then, as much as possible, use domestic products for all buildings, equipment, stationery, and appliances in the school, so that there are no foreign goods left in the entire school and it becomes a purely domestic consumer place.

Second, we should also use the effectiveness of education itself to create a psychology among students of loving domestic products, stimulate their self-esteem, and know that blindly worshiping foreign goods is wrong and shameful. The compilation of national products teaching materials, the promotion of national products speeches at gatherings, and the transfer of production skills and knowledge are all necessary products for the implementation of "national products education."

In short. Our education community is the leader of the students. In this "Student National Products Year," the responsibility lies with you, and there is no room for shirking. You should stand in front of the students and work hard for the future of domestic products!

The above four items are only contributed by using the valuable space of the Shen Bao National Products Weekly. I hope everyone can discuss them more. I think: it is not without considerable relationship to the entire "Student National Products Year" domestic products movement.

How Various Countries are Resisting Japanese Goods After Loving Domestic Products

— Yin Ge

(I) Intensification of Economic Nationalism After the European War, the international economic phenomenon that deserves attention is the strengthening of economic nationalism. Advocated by Mr. Wilson, the Treaty of Versailles, which was concluded, saw the emergence of several new countries. These countries, based on the principle of national self-determination, formed independent nations. However, from an economic perspective, they lacked the necessary conditions for independent countries. In order to make up for their shortcomings, they encouraged domestic production and excluded foreign goods, thus concretizing economic nationalism.

The United States originally practiced protectionism, making it a nation of economic nationalism. After the Great War, this ideology was further strengthened. Everyone loved domestic products and continued to increase tariffs to block the import of foreign goods. Countries like Germany and France are old nations in Europe. The strategy for managing post-war affairs was based on economic nationalism. Although Britain is the birthplace of free trade, its economic policy has also changed in recent years. It has continued to raise tariffs on the import of foreign goods. From this perspective, this situation is quite evident among countries. Now, let's explain the situation of tariff increases in major countries around the world as follows:

In 1930, the United States' import value was 3 billion gold dollars. The tariff collected was 480 million gold dollars, accounting for 15.9% of the import value. However, two years later, in 1932, the import value was 1.3 billion gold dollars, while the tariff collected was 260 million gold dollars, accounting for 20% of the import value. This means that the US tax has already been raised.

In 1930, Britain's import value was 1.04 billion pounds. The tariff revenue was 120 million pounds, with a ratio of 11.6%. In 1932, the import value was 700 million pounds. The tariff revenue was 160 million pounds, with a ratio to the import value of 23.1%. This means that Britain's tariff has increased from 11.6% to 23.1%. The ratio of French tariff revenue to the import value was 8% in 1930 and increased to 18.3% in 1932. In 1930, Japan's import value was 1.54 billion yuan. The tariff revenue was 110 million yuan, with a ratio of 7.3%. By 1932, the import value was 1.42 billion yuan. The tariff revenue was 106 million yuan, with a ratio of 7.5%. The tariff increase was minimal.

The competition among countries to increase tariffs and build economic barriers against other countries is an important reason for the decline in global trade. Therefore, an economic conference was held in London last June to solve the difficulties. At this conference, the United States and the European gold standard group had conflicting opinions on the issue of exchange rate stability, which eventually led to a breakdown. The fundamental reason for the failure of this conference was the strong economic nationalism prevailing among countries, which made it impossible to ease. Since the breakdown of this conference, the budding of international coordination has been crushed again, and economic nationalism has become even more intense.

(II) Japan's Position on the International Trade Front From the above situation, it can be seen that excluding foreign goods and encouraging domestic production is almost a common situation in the world today. Japan's position in the international community is particularly special. There are two reasons for this. Firstly, Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations due to the Manchurian Incident caused resentment in various countries. Secondly, the value of the Japanese Yen has fallen abnormally, making Japanese goods particularly cheap. Japan is not afraid of economic blockades by various countries after its withdrawal from the League of Nations. This is because the disadvantages of economic blockades often lie with the opposing countries, not Japan. For example, if the United States does not sell cotton to Japan, the loser will still be the United States. Therefore, economic severance is quite difficult to implement. However, slow economic pressure can be achieved on individual issues, such as economic negotiations between Britain and Japan. The decline in the Japanese Yen has a more significant impact on international pressure. The degree of resistance to it by various countries is even greater than its withdrawal from the League of Nations. For example, the economic relations between Britain and Japan, such as the Indian trade treaty issue and the increase in tariffs on cotton cloth, all stem from this.

The Path to Survival for Domestic Goods

— Da Bu

Someone asked: "Why haven't there been significant achievements in the two years of promoting domestic goods?" This question made me think about the path to survival for domestic goods.

Where is the path to survival for domestic goods? (1) In publicity: In recent years, the establishment of domestic goods companies everywhere has led to considerable sales, which should be the effect of publicity; (2) In imitation: Anyone who has been to a domestic goods company will naturally see a lot of domestic goods, and the achievements in imitation can be described as outstanding; (3) In cultivating talents for researching domestic goods raw materials, this work should be assigned to research institutes in the highest institutions or organizations like scientific societies; For example, our tung oil is originally a large export commodity. If foreign countries plant tung trees now, the future harvest will be our loss. Relying on foreign goods as raw materials is not a long-term plan; (4) In establishing large-scale factories; For example, many highways have been built in various provinces, and the means of transportation rely entirely on foreign goods, which is not a good solution. We should also have a car factory like the Russian Stalin Factory, manufacturing completely domestic cars. Similarly, there should also be large-scale aircraft factories, manufacturing completely domestic aircraft; This great work should be founded by the government or jointly by officials and businessmen; (5) In invention: New inventions can not only wash away our Chinese people's shame of not being able to create miracles, but also have a good opportunity to promote sales abroad. Although this item is listed last, it is the most important.

Looking at it this way, I dare to answer the initial question; The failure in the past two years is because only the first two points mentioned above have been done, and the rest have not been achieved. Even if the last item has factual evidence, those inventors may be trapped by financial resources, so we have not yet seen their harvest, which is really a pity!

News

Doctor Brand Soap Sells Well

Doctor Brand Soap is produced by Tianjin Zhongchang Soap Factory. The manager of the factory, Mr. Shi Dongchu, once studied in Europe and has a wealth of experience. Considering that soap is a daily necessity, and the climate in South China is hot and humid, bathing and washing require even more soap than elsewhere. If our compatriots all use imported products, the loss of interests will be alarming. Therefore, he carefully researched and used purely domestic raw materials to mechanically produce various soaps. Up to now, it has been 20 years, and after government investigation and examination by the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce, it has been confirmed as a purely complete and excellent domestic product, and a certificate of protection has been specially issued. The soaps produced by the factory, totaling 70 or 80 kinds, are all of excellent quality, pure and fragrant, and have special effects on protecting health. In the 22nd year of the Republic of China, the factory established business offices on the second floor of Jiufu Company at No. 5 Ma Road in the Shanghai British Concession, and in Changfeng Bank on Haopan Street in Guangzhou to expand sales and facilitate procurement.

Multi-filament Light Bulb - A New Invention by Mr. Qiu Boan, a Young Chinese Man

— Yu

During this year of promoting domestic goods, the new invention of multi-filament light bulbs by young Mr. Qiu Boan is a truly gratifying event! The multi-filament light bulb has been on the market for several months, and users in this and other cities have consistently praised it. Therefore, the business is becoming increasingly prosperous, and the supply cannot meet the demand. It is recalled that at the opening of the distribution office on Daxin Street, someone presented the inscription "The Light of Domestic Goods". Looking at it today, it is truly not an empty reputation.

The biggest feature of the multi-filament light bulb is its economy. Its manufacturing combines three or two filaments of different wattage into one, which can be activated in sequence. It is equipped with a mechanism that can be used to activate any number of filaments at will, hence the name "multi-filament." Even if one filament breaks, the other filaments remain intact and can still be used. If there are three filaments, one bulb is equivalent to three bulbs; if there are two filaments, it is equivalent to two bulbs. The bulb will only be discarded when all three or two filaments are broken. However, the second feature of the multi-filament light bulb is its durability. The filaments do not break easily; other bulbs are discarded first. Moreover, the multi-filament light bulb is not afraid of severe vibrations.

The first batch of products still had a flaw, which was that before installing the bulb, the switch had to be turned off before it could be activated, which was a bit of a hassle. After the second batch, research and improvements have been made, and it is no longer necessary to turn off the switch first, which is more convenient for users. Therefore, the increasing prosperity of its business is a matter of expectation, not accidental.

Short Story

A Year's Effort (Part 1)

— Ye Qibai

(I) The Beginning of Awakening

I went back to my village for three days and happily spent the Lunar New Year at home; now I'm back at school again, time really flies! My mother's loving face seems to be still in front of my eyes.

Imagining that during the holidays, many classmates went home; how lonely this school and this dormitory must have been! But now it has returned to the same liveliness and the same joy as in the past.

My classmate Tao and I were sitting at the desk in the bedroom, he was writing his diary, and I was writing an unfinished manuscript.

"Ji Ge, Ji Ge," suddenly, there was the sound of leather shoes walking, getting closer and closer. From the rhythm of this shoe sound, we could tell that it was our good friend He coming.

"Ah! It's probably Lao He coming." I put down my pen, took the thermos, and poured hot water to drink; I said this to Lao Tao.

Lao Tao didn't speak, just nodded to me; and Lao He had already walked into the room.

A very spirited young man in a suit; curly hair, face so fair and lovely; snow-white scarf, inlaid in the collar of the black coat, the black and white, set off the harmonious brightness; the suit pants, straight, covered the back of the leather shoes, and revealed the shiny pointed leather shoe toes.

"Oh! Lao He! What did you buy? In that paper bag," I said.

"Isn't it food?" Tao also asked.

He opened the paper bag with a smile. Several exquisite cosmetics were revealed in the green oily wrapping paper. What Pond's Cold Cream, what Si Dan Kang, what ×××'s hair styling gel, ............ all imported cosmetics.

"Lao He! Where did you buy these things?" I asked.

"Oh! I watched a play with Miss Li at the Paris Theater and bought them on Avenue Joffre: I only bought a little bit myself, and bought a lot for Miss Li! Oh! The foreign girls in that department store are really beautiful! The attitude is so kind to hand the things to me, and send us out." He said this very proudly.

"But, you have to know, what kind of stuff is this?" Tao pulled and asked.

"Of course it's imported goods!" He said arrogantly.

"Then, you should know that this year is Student Domestic Goods Year! Why do you still buy foreign goods; and, it's consumable foreign goods?" Tao asked again.

"Oh! I know that. But, you have to forgive me, in front of a girlfriend, if I don't do this, it would be a stingy and shameful thing!" He replied.

"Ha! You're wrong, do you think buying these imported cosmetics will enhance your love; and going to the domestic goods company to buy domestic cosmetics will diminish your love? I don't think so, and if there are domestic goods to buy, buying them as gifts is a glorious and happy thing!" Tao said a lot again.

He nodded, silently, expressing endless guilt, and had nothing more to argue. And I just sat in silence; thinking, He is awake. So, I broke the temporary silence and said: (To be continued)
