Free Talk

Trivial Talks on Historical Essays (I)

— Cao Juren

Literature and history are twin sisters in China. European and Western academics have always been included in philosophy; in China, all academics originate from history. Ancient and modern literati often steal tricks from the Records of the Grand Historian and the Book of Han. Gui Youguang, the ancestor of the Tongcheng School, was an ancient essayist who read the Records of the Grand Historian with a five-colored pen; Zhang Shizhai also wrote a book like "Wen Shi Tong Yi" that connected literature and history. Not only ancient essayists, but also pure literary writers are like this: Sima Qian's Biography of Xiang Yu vividly describes the siege of Gaixia. Tang and Song poets used this theme to compose epic poems, and playwrights used this theme to create dramas. Now there is still Mei Lanfang playing "Farewell My Concubine", which is quite popular. Historical figures such as Zhu Maichen, Wang Zhaojun, and Yang Guifei are also written in this way and that way, with various ideologies changing with the times. Someone discussed the issue of literary property in previous years; If we want to say that China has any precious literary heritage, I think it is definitely not ancient essays or parallel prose; history is one of the valuable heritages.

Since the May Fourth Movement, biographical literature has declined, and chapter novels with historical stories as themes have also declined. The new novels influenced by European and American literature are completely different from chapter novels in terms of skills and consciousness; Some people have also put new coats on historical figures, such as Guo Moruo's "Three Rebellious Women" and Wang Duqing's "Yang Guifei", which can only be said to be small ripples in the literary craze and are not noticed by the general public. Mao Dun also wrote several short historical novels such as "Dazexiang" and "Shijie" after the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, but the impact was not significant; Until now, only Liu Shengdan's excavation is a purely historical collection. Recently, with the development of essays, some people have paid attention to the development of historical essays. Last month, a female art group sent someone to see me and said that there are three emerging essay styles: humorous essays, scientific essays, and historical essays, with historical essays being the most noticed by them. This may be a sign that biographical literature and historical novels are making a comeback.

I started writing historical essays inspired by the Japanese Ryunosuke Akutagawa. The three pieces of Akutagawa Ryunosuke's essays read in Xie Liuyi's translation of Japanese essay selections all used Chinese historical events: 1. "The Device of a Hero" was written using the stories of Xiang Yu Benji Lu Ma Dong; 2. "Weisheng's Letter" was written using the story of Weisheng in the Records of the Grand Historian; 3. "Yellow Millet Dream" was written using the story of Lusheng in the Tang Dynasty legend. Once decorated, ancient stories appear in the current era with a very new posture, and I feel a very strong interest. For example, at the end of "Yellow Millet Dream", it says: "Xu Sheng listened intently to Lu Weng's words, and when he asked his opponent carefully, he raised his youthful face and said with a glint in his eyes: 'Because this is a dream, I still want to live, like the awakening of that dream, this dream will come when it awakens! When that time comes, I still want to live a true life, don't you think so?'" This modern spirit is as bright as the sun, making me very happy. Following his candle light, reading the history books I have read in the past, new meanings flash everywhere. Three years ago, I started writing this kind of essay.

Small Scene of Huaiyuan

— Shen Shengshi

For the sake of life, I traveled far from Jiangnan to Huaiyuan.

Huaiyuan is a small county town in northern Anhui. It is about twenty-five miles upstream from Bengbu. If Huaiyuan is a county town, it really doesn't look like one; If you compare it with Kunshan, Suzhou in Jiangnan, this place only has the style of a town.

The streets are all paved with uneven mountain stones. It is even more difficult to walk in the rain. There is no prosperous market, nor any large shops with decent scale; At night, there are no street lights, nor any night markets; After ten o'clock, I sit quietly in the room, listening to the watchman beating the big bronze gong on the dark streets. From the loud sound of the gong, you can hear the desolation of this county town.

Under the scene of such a gray street scene, after you run through it once, you won't want to walk it a second time.

Just take a casual look at the street to see the poverty of this place. In front of the board tables at the door of some very small restaurants, one or two sallow-faced men are sitting there chewing a piece of dark wheat cake with relish. Such a life is really fatal for southerners.

However, most of the people here live on this stuff. Those who eat rice are a minority and a minority of the upper class, but it is only the crudest steamed rice mixed with millet.

This small city is surrounded by mountains on three sides. Although there is no beautiful scenery, the natural scenery is enough to watch. At sunset, the sun sets from the waist of the mountain, and the red light reflects the snow-covered mountain tops; Watching a crow in the evening, croaking and flapping its dark wings and flying back. At this time, a homesickness like light clouds comes to touch your heart.

Burning a cigarette, sitting silently by the window, listening to the vulgar and annoying gongs and drums of the street performers; Carefully taste the life and scenery of this place, and think like an idiot, the old China is so desolate and pitiful everywhere!

February 13, 1935, at Huaizhong, Huaiyuan

Science and Literature

— Bo Han

Combining literature and science does not seem to be a recent topic. Since the great development of natural science in the nineteenth century, naturalism in literature has flourished greatly. Those naturalist writers undoubtedly tried their best to use the achievements of science in literature. Now, in our literary world, we hear the call to combine science and literature again. Is it to relive the old dreams of the nineteenth century? I think it's not that simple.

After reading the content of the natural science essays mentioned on Free Talk a few days ago, and talking about the penetration of natural science and literature, I thought that there are two tendencies in this. For example, the article "On the Penetration of Natural Science and Literature" is based on the standpoint of emphasizing literature, and its intention is to apply scientific methods to literature, but the article "The Content of Natural Science Essays" emphasizes the content of science. Originally, the newly emerging scientific essay is a kind of thing that uses literary brushstrokes to talk about science, and the focus is on science.

The rise of scientific essays like this is undoubtedly a new trend. Because of this, we can say that today's mention of science and literature getting married is not to relive the old dreams of the nineteenth century.

But according to the principle that content determines form, then, taking natural scientific facts as content, naturally, it is necessary to adopt that kind of cumbersome and dry form in order to meticulously and economically record the products of human reason without omission. This is the origin of general scientific writing. But literary writing is a concrete expression of human life, human thoughts, and emotions. Its content is living people and the logical development of their behavior. Therefore, it has another form, so moving and thought-provoking. Now, we want to express the content of science in the form of literature. Isn't it a difficult task to "climb a tree to catch a fish"?

What can be expressed in the form of literature is only the scientific ideas, theories and work. I think that the activities of people should still be the center, and science should be integrated. The so-called scientific ideas are performing and implying in the activities of various characters, and scientific work is of course not a rigid report of work results, but a lively description of the work process. The selection of content should not be arbitrarily dividing scientific records into fragments and using them to fill the number, but connecting important scientific ideas with the real society and expressing them in a literary way.

Cattle and Horse Row

— Xicun

There is a road in Jilin called -- Cattle and Horse Row.

Please think about this name. Interesting, isn't it?

Of course, you think that there are mostly "cattle" and "horses" on the row, but you will soon regret that you are thinking wrong; How can a street have mostly "cattle" and "horses" walking and fewer humans? A street is always opened for the convenience of traffic, and it is definitely not built for the sake of walking cattle and horses. So, you guess again, thinking: Maybe it is a place to comment on the market conditions of cattle and horses and talk about buying and selling? In other words, should there be a "cattle and horse market" attached? Yes, my opinion is exactly the same as yours. However, it must be said that although we guess the same and it is very reasonable, in reality, the situation of Cattle and Horse Row is completely different. Even if this street was originally named as we guessed, however, in recent years, there has been no such thing.

"So, what kind of street is Cattle and Horse Row?"

You can't help but ask me this way. Yes, I should explain it to you, so as not to make you shake your head at this interesting name.

Friends, haven't you been to the City God Temple in Shanghai? Okay, this saves me a lot of trouble in words. Let me tell you, the situation of Cattle and Horse Row in Jilin is the same as the area near the City God Temple in Shanghai. Cattle and horses are naturally not lacking, but they do not become a (market), but run to do the work of pulling carts and transporting goods. So, let me tell you, "Cattle and Horse" Row is exactly where "people" walk. It's quite interesting to compare people to cattle and horses. In fact, to be honest, why can't people "be compared to" cattle and horses? No, why aren't people "are" cattle and horses? Everyone, running around every day, the situation is the same as the running of cattle and horses.

Cattle and Horse Row is a very wide street. The City God Temple is at the southwest end, but the temple is only for people to burn incense and worship. As for the rest of the shops, large and small, they are not in the temple. Going out of the City God Temple and turning north along the street, look: blacksmith shops, flames and dust swirling around, and small vendors selling small toys along the street. Then there are pawnshops, shoe shops, and food shops. Further on, there is a labor market, where you will see groups of poor people waiting together for employers to come. They don't look like humans, but like a pile of goods for people to choose from. The vegetable building is built in the middle of the street, and this is where expensive vegetables are sold. In winter, you can buy cucumbers and eggplants, as long as you are willing to spend more money. Not far behind, another area is created, like a square garden, which is called the "Antique Market". There are indeed some antiques, but I don't know the goods and can't say much about the names, but in this "Antique Market", the second-hand clothes sellers shouted while stomping their feet. But the shouting sounds they shout are rhythmic songs. Listen, I'll write you a set of short songs:

"This good fur coat

Five thousand nine hundred and thirty diaos,

It's good to wear,

The hair won't fall out for five or six years."

Continuing north, to the south of the north city wall, there is the big vegetable market, which is really lively in the morning. There are many grain stores and hotels, all of which are doing business in winter. In winter, the vehicles and horses of the villages that come to the city to sell grain all have to live in these inns.

A Cattle and Horse Row street is busy all day long. The people and horses coming and going are running around together. Shouting, the sound of restaurants calling seats and knocking spoons, the sound of iron tools banging, the sound of street performers striking gongs, the sound of female drummers shouting and singing... are mixed together and released in all directions, releasing priceless miscellaneous music.

In Cattle and Horse Row, you can't see fashionable women, you can't find fashionable women, you can't find elegant scholars who taste tea and chat. The characters who come and go are just living a little better than cattle and horses. The name Cattle and Horse Row is still in use, please think about it, isn't this name also not unsuitable?

Robbery

— Ding Lang

Having suffered someone's oversight, scattered yellow soybeans are all over the ground; the cold wind turns up hunched and tattered clothes, five or six children, more than ten hands busy on the ground.

A car sped past, emitting a cloud of grinding, sandy green smoke; embracing the dust, they can't fill their own bags, only regretting why they didn't break a few more burlap sacks? No one cares about this, each goes his own way. Casting a white eye, expressing indifference!

Heaven only gave two hands, otherwise they could scoop it all up; everyone jostles, unable to compete with the elderly.

Dusk (3)

— Qu Yi

Finally, they walked onto Xinsheng Road. They turned right. A gust of wind blew at the corner. The short one hastily straightened his clothes, casually buttoning a button, pulling the long shirt down even further, shortening his legs by another inch. The tall one took two strides, putting the short one behind him.

Xinsheng Road still insists on maintaining its dignity, putting on the airs of a major metropolis in central China. The electric lights are blindingly bright. Outside each shop, various dazzling red and green colors—either advertising posters or sample fabrics—are used to decorate their aging appearance. But every few shops, there is always a shop with its door half-closed, or completely sealed with a white "for rent" sign, puncturing the vanity of this Xinsheng Road that so desperately wants to save face.

However, Xinsheng Road is, after all, glorious, and is, after all, lively. The people on the sidewalks are jostling each other. As soon as the sound of leather shoes passes by, a large group of "road inspectors" of all ages, looking emaciated, surround it. At the same time, cries of "Master! Young master! Sir!" also chase after the "clip-clop, clip-clop" of the leather shoes.

The tall one's leather shoes sounded loudly on Xinsheng Road. The road inspectors followed him as usual. All the more separating the short one behind, even though the short one quickened his short legs, he could only see a particularly prominent black head floating on the "sea of heads."

"Damn!" The black head suddenly stopped floating. He cursed. The short one, then, quickened his steps, immediately charged into the crowd, and rejoined the tall one, becoming a matching pair.

"Not easy!" he said, "So walking the whole country is impossible. At this rate, it will take ten years to walk half of Xinsheng Road!"

"Damn! It's best to—" The tall one's mouth and leather shoes made sounds at the same time, sounding loud and rhythmic. "Shoot them one by one! Then the world will be at peace. This bunch of Chinese! Chinese! When I was in Japan—"

"Hey! Hey! Move!" Immediately, a voice of expulsion came from across the street. Look, a dark brown policeman is walking towards them. He is dispersing the road inspectors! "Still not moving! You street ghosts! Hey! Hey!..."

"Clip-clop! Clip-clop! Clip-clop!" Also the sound of leather shoes, majestic and powerful! Immediately, he drove the wandering souls into the alleys in groups of three or four: some even flew to the garbage cans at the entrances of the alleys like flies chasing after a foul smell, grabbing, patting, searching for discarded rice grains and bones.

"After all—" The tall one patted the short one on the shoulder. "China isn't going to perish after all! There are still a few people maintaining order. When I was in Japan!"

"Hmm!" This time, the short one had nothing to say. He seemed to feel some sadness. The policeman and his partner both wore leather shoes. They walked with energy and authority. Only he wore rubber shoes! Walking along, it sounded like an old toothless woman muttering a curse.

"However—" But another thought crossed his mind. "Walking is lighter with these rubber shoes! Although my wallet is also in bad shape. But—"

"But which way should we turn now!" The tall one stopped at the entrance of Xinsheng Road.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

The German Sex Spy Case

— Feng

Last month, a sex spy case occurred in Japan, in which many noble women were in love with a foreign military officer, and they did not hesitate to search for information and secretly contribute it to him. As a result, one of the women reported to the authorities because her request was not fulfilled, and the case was broken. Unexpectedly, a similar case has recently occurred in Germany. It is romantic and extremely sensational, like material from a novel. The protagonist is Mrs. Von Bülow, and Mrs. Nazena has been sentenced to death. It is truly a case of like minds think alike.

It is said that the truth of the case is that Baroness von Bülow met a Polish military officer who loved gambling and riding, and was beautiful and charming. The Baroness fell in love with him and could not extricate herself, and was willing to run around and find military secrets for him. What was particularly vicious was that the Baroness made many women at social events, indulged in drinking, and introduced them to young men. The women with weak will would have illicit affairs with them, and the Baroness would secretly take their photos and show them to their daughters. Thus, for the sake of their faces, the women had no choice but to obey her orders. Her use of schemes was unparalleled.

The art of war says that if you know yourself and your enemy, you will win every battle. If you want to know your enemy, you cannot do without spies. In the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods of our country, diplomacy was rampant, the strong annexed the weak, so the art of espionage was quite researched. In recent years, the world has become interconnected, and the law of the jungle prevails, which is the same as in the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods, so the art of espionage also has an unfathomable aspect. Sun Tzu's "The Use of Spies" says that there are five types of spies: native spies, inside spies, double spies, expendable spies, and living spies. Inside spies are those who are employed from among the enemy's officials. Therefore, the German sex spy case is also a type of inside spy. Because female spies had not yet been invented at that time, Sun Tzu did not explain it, but he said that one cannot obtain the truth of espionage without subtlety. One must be divine and adaptable, which depends on human effort.

In recent years, many countries have used women as spies, firstly, because women's actions rarely involve politics, so people do not pay much attention to them. Secondly, beautiful women are easily infatuated by men with sexual desires, and domestic secrets are often easily exposed unconsciously. Nowadays, countries are opening up new frontiers and using handsome men as spies, so that women with sexual desires are infatuated with military uniforms and leather boots, and obey their lovers' commands. This method of espionage is truly full of wonders.

Baroness von Bülow and Mrs. Nazena, because they were infatuated with a Polish military officer, did not hesitate to secretly leak the German plan to invade Poland. The seriousness of their crimes is self-evident, and being sentenced to death is their just desert. However, Germany used an axe to behead the two women, instead of shooting or electrocuting them, which is not the behavior of a civilized country. Therefore, the British newspaper criticized it as a "revival of medieval barbaric behavior," which cannot be said to be an excessive criticism.

×× Chronicle

— Bing

×× is a native of Jiangbei. He is a university professor and has a considerable status in society; he is indeed "my friend," and a very good one at that, which is truly fortunate. Because we are very good friends, I have explained to him several times that I want to give him a quick sketch and submit it to the newspaper. At first, he flatly denied it, but later he couldn't resist me and reluctantly agreed, but he said, "Friend, no matter what, don't announce my name!" This is the origin of the code name ××.

Just being a university professor is not so special. ×× has a special quality. Just focusing on his daily life, describing it would be a very long article. There is too much material. Here, I can only "extract the essence and select the finest" and briefly go through it.

His daily life is full of romance, but he is not a researcher of literature, but an educational mentor. His living room is disorganized beyond description. From the beginning of the semester to the vacation, the two greasy and pungent cotton quilts on the bed are never folded. Books and magazines are piled all over the bed, no, he simply tramples on the books. There are also books on the table, books on the floor, and of course even more in the corners. Books, very messy books, are scattered all over the room. In addition, there are countless cigarette butts. Speaking of cigarettes, they really seem to be his life. He has two deep ashtrays, one placed on the desk and the other placed next to his pillow. When reading and writing, he smokes non-stop, and he always smokes a few cigarettes before going to bed. He often says that he can eat less rice, but he must smoke more cigarettes. If you talk to him for less than a quarter of an hour, he will smoke at least three cigarettes in a row.

However, it is indeed strange that his work and rest are very regular. He goes to bed every night at eight o'clock (at the latest nine o'clock) and gets up before six o'clock in the morning, which is a devout follower of the New Life Movement.

As for talking about things outside of his daily life, that is truly a waste of words.

He often says: "Our Jiangbei dialect, although it doesn't sound very good, is easy to learn. But the Shanghai dialect is really not easy to learn. I have been in 'this place' for five whole years, and I only know the two words 'fire speed, fire speed.' These two words are very useful when taking a car to exchange copper coins or buying things in a store. As soon as I say them, people know that I am not a country bumpkin, and I get a lot of advantages."

Page 22

He wore his straw hat until late autumn before it disappeared. One day, he suddenly changed to a new felt hat, but the felt hat was extremely clumsy. Looking at it, it was at most a one-dollar item. I was very surprised and questioned him: "Mr. ××, how can a university professor wear such a cheap felt hat?" This triggered his chatter, and he said so eloquently: "I have also worn wool hats that cost five or six yuan, and I have also worn felt hats that cost more than ten yuan, but they were always robbed. How were they robbed? I was sitting in a rickshaw, and the rickshaw puller ran forward quickly. I was careless, and the hat on my head was grabbed and taken away. I jumped out of the car to chase, but they were gone like a crane in the yellow sky. So now I only buy felt hats that cost one yuan, which is much more reassuring. I can wear one for two years without losing it, and it's even more cost-effective."

I have never seen his virtuous wife. According to his own confession, she is a typical rural yellow-faced woman, but he loves her very much. He writes her at least three letters a week, and they are written in the most sweet way. Once, I walked quietly into his room and stood behind him. He was writing a love letter to his wife. The opening sentences were: "×: It has been raining these days in this place, and it has been raining heavily, so my heart is troubled. I miss you all the time!..."

Therefore, I often talk to him about women, which makes him very happy. When we talk about it, he is simply endless. When he is happy, he always says "ha ha, ha ha, incredibly". But he also tries his best to express his respect for women. He says that he has never flirted with a second woman except for his own wife. During the January 28th Incident, he and a female friend were trapped in a warehouse together. That woman simply acted wildly towards him, but he held back and did not do anything. He only said that when he was working in a ×× organization, a female colleague asked him for an abortion prescription, and he only flirted with her a few times, but it was not important.

××'s interesting stories are really too many to tell, so let's stop here!

Listening to the Wind

— Jing Jia

Recently, I have developed a hobby of listening to the wind, which is formed by the environment. For the past few years, I have lived in the countryside by the sea. There are no high mountains in the vast fields, so the sea breeze can sing freely around my house. Morning, noon, dusk, late at night, it is always playing on my eardrums. So, I have developed a hobby of listening to the wind—in fact, even if I don't want to listen, I have to listen.

I feel that the music of the wind is extremely magnificent. Perhaps the shouts of killing on the battlefield are no more than that? Sometimes I am tired, so I light a cigarette and lean on the window frame, putting my ears on the glass window. Then I can be happy for a while, and even sad or annoying things will be forgotten. The sound of the wind gives me a lot of comfort.

Since I have this hobby, I hope that the music of the wind will not be interrupted. I hope for the arrival of the wind as eagerly as I hope for food.

However, one day I finally discovered my own selfishness. I saw a poor farmer in his fifties or sixties walking slowly on the road. His hands were in his sleeves, his head was shrunk, and the roaring wind blew off the broken strips hanging on his tattered clothes. Immediately, I knew that he was being bullied by the wind, while I was the one who was enjoying the wind! I was indeed sinful. I thought that the wind was not for me to enjoy. The rich enjoy the snow, and the beggars freeze to death, it's all the same thing. I am not rich, I should not forget others!

So I cut off my hobby of listening to the wind.

Taoye Ferry

— Hou Hu

Taoye Ferry will never be erased from the memory of my life. It was four years ago, on a silent moonlit night in late autumn, I came out from a small wine shop after drinking alone. Probably because of my fondness for it! Although the wine filled my head, I still stumbled along the road to the Taoye Ferry, the "land of Six Dynasties gold dust." The sky was covered with glittering stars, and the Wende Bridge across the Qinhuai River, and the willows swaying on both banks of the river, seemed to accompany my lonely heart, but I didn't see a single Taoye leaf. I timidly held onto the railing and looked down at the flowing water of the Qinhuai River. I thought that because the houses on both sides were high and dense, the river seemed more solemn and profound than our city river. The black water of the river reflected the bright moonlight, making it even more mysterious. The windows of the river houses on both sides were closed quietly, and there was probably a plank railing outside the windows, fully showing the flavor of the water towns of Jiangnan. I looked far away at the mountain peaks of Zhongshan covered with moonlight, and further imagined the scenery of the Qinhuai River flowing into the countryside ten miles away, and I couldn't help but recite the ancient poem "To this day, only Jiangshan is green, Qin is only blue," a poem lamenting the past. Thinking of the prosperous scene of the Qinhuai River in "The Scholars," with "ten miles of pearl curtains, singing and painted boats," compared to the quiet houses in front of me, the cool moonlight, and the dark river, how could I not be filled with desolate and sentimental thoughts!

Taking advantage of the moonlight, I walked across the bridge and went to the pile of low bungalows. The streets were narrow and medieval, and the double doors of the houses on both sides were mostly nailed with animal hinges and copper rings, and pasted with red paper couplets, fully showing the colors of the northern city—even though it was still in Jiangnan—but the loveliness and memorableness of this ancient city lies in these ordinary and simple places! I walked around in circles, humming ancient famous poems, trying to grasp the loveliness of this scenic spot from my marrow, and also wanted to find a few local elders to ask about the rise and fall of this ferry, but the doors of the houses were closed quietly, and the owls on the trees made strange cries that made people's hair stand on end, as if saying that it was late at night. Walking back along the river, turning my head every step of the way. On the way, I passed a narrow and winding alley, with a sign that said "Ancient Fishing Alley." It turned out that this was the ancient alley of the capital's boundless spring scenery. Since ancient times, this has been a place of orioles and flowers. Its mystery is no less than that of the North Sichuan Road, Shanghai's "Mystery Street." It contains infinite romantic stories from ancient times to the present, but the charm of this place is ancient, lush, elegant, and contained in the bones, which is completely different from the naked scene of North Sichuan Road. I can only wait for a chance in the future to come back to this ancient alley to see the peach blossoms and faces!

The Only Way Out for Rural Women

— A Fool's Words

Morning

— Feng

It has almost become my habit that even if I sleep late, I will always wake up when the east is slightly bright. In a corner like the one I live in, it is really quiet enough; if you want to sleep, you can sleep quietly in the cool air of the morning, but you can't; every day when the crows fly over the roof, I will always wake up, and I have finally breathed enough of the morning air. I forgot who said that people who live in the city don't have mornings, and people who can't see the morning are pitiful; so, waking up early is very happy.

I am not from the city. Country people get up early, and I am also quite fond of the country morning, and I like to be busy in the morning: especially after many years of city life, I especially love the country morning. In the countryside, I can't bear to sleep in the morning. When I hear the rooster crowing for the third time, like a child who wants to get up to wear new clothes for the New Year, I will get up, and sometimes I will walk around in the lower crescent moon, attracting the dogs in the village to bark: I have tasted the taste of "the bright moon surrounds the quiet room" in the morning. In fact, not only is the room quiet, but everything is very quiet, there is movement in the quiet, there is vitality: oh, it is so full of life, whose door is open, in the faint light, you can hear people talking, but you can't see people; these are all very fond of me, but there are no them in the city, the city morning seems to have not attracted anyone's attention, even the people in the city don't have a morning.

Morning seems to be destined for me. After I became a city dweller, I still saw a lot of mornings in the city.

I like the sound of pushcarts or large carts rolling over the streets in the morning. Rumble. Rumble, rumble, very nice to hear, that sound will drive away all evil thoughts from people, will arouse the courage of lazy people, and move forward in that advancing sound. It's really like a piece of music that shows the tide attacking the rocks, a layer of waves rushes up, retreats, quiets down, and moves away; the second layer rushes up again, and it's the same way, tick-tick-tick, the tone goes from high to low, and moves away again. Every morning, my alley always rings like that, and when the sun smears the treetops, that sound disappears. After this, the sound of the almond tea pot lid rings, and it is transmitted from the alley. In the cool air of the morning, you can see the water vapor rising from afar, and a group of people are drinking so busily around the tea pot; after finishing, they put down their bowls, and the almond tea is picked to another place, and the alley begins to quiet down. The quiet after a rush often makes me feel lonely. Open the curtains and look at the morning sun, the gray roof tiles, even in the morning air, the color is still so gray; the only thing that can comfort me is the sparrows bathing and leaping on the neighbor's withered locust tree. The morning in the city is over like this, and when the hooligans carrying birdcages sing strange tunes in the alley, in the countryside, the sun can already warm your back.

However, it is still unfortunate that when I knew that getting up early was a blessing, I was already a city dweller. In the countryside, getting up early is a habit, but that is a blessing, that must be what city people say. Country people only know how to get up early, but they don't know that getting up early is a blessing; city people can say that getting up early is a blessing, but in reality they don't have a morning. These are two groups of people, and their lives may be distinguished in this place. I am a countryman in the city, I know this.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

Mary Pickford on the Secrets of Movie Star Success (Part 2)

— Zhu Tong

Mary Pickford also said that one should not take a setback too seriously. A loss may turn out to be a blessing in disguise. She said: "Once, we wanted to hire Charles Farrell to co-star with me in a film. But later we didn't use him and replaced him with someone else. Charles was inevitably disappointed and sad. I called him in and told him that we didn't use him not because he couldn't act, but because another person's style was more suitable. A week later, Fox offered him to co-star with Janet Gaynor in "Seventh Heaven". He became famous overnight in "Seventh Heaven". If we had used him beforehand, the results might not have been as impressive as "Seventh Heaven".

"Don't go out socializing too often. Your time is extremely precious, so avoid all unnecessary social engagements as much as possible. Always prioritize your career. If you have free time, you should use it to prepare yourself and develop your talents in all aspects, even in the smallest areas. French or Italian can improve your diction and give you a wider range in your speech. I am still learning French myself. I will also learn some Italian soon.

"Get at least eight hours of sleep every day. It is best to sleep eight and a half hours every day. Try to make yourself feel refreshed in the morning so that your healthy beauty is reflected in your face. You should treat the time after 10 p.m. every night as belonging to your career if you haven't gotten a job, or as belonging to the company if you already have a job. This way, you won't waste that precious sleep time.

"While it is important to maintain strict self-discipline, you must not be too harsh on yourself. Personal enjoyment, within a reasonable range, is indispensable. You should treat yourself as you would treat your little sister. You should often talk to yourself and point out all your mistakes. You can also apologize to yourself if you have done something wrong and promise not to do it again. You may make the same mistake a second time, but never make the same mistake three times in a row. If you keep making mistakes one after another, then you are really incorrigibly foolish. No one is perfect. Moreover, without mistakes, there is no progress. One is never too old to learn. I always gain new experiences and new insights every day. But there are many things that you don't need to experience yourself, you can learn from others.

"Avoid all disreputable publicity. The status of stars does not come from disreputable publicity. Even when you are humble and unknown, you must never use disreputable publicity to get people to hear your name. Otherwise, she will eventually regret it. Many famous women in Hollywood share my view on this point.

"While you are in Hollywood, don't let your thinking become outdated. You should have a good understanding of art, literature, politics, etc. Many people have lived in Hollywood for too long, and their thoughts, conversations, and actions are all limited by their work, resulting in them becoming mechanical figures whose words are dull and tasteless. Good hobbies are also essential for everyone. They can give you new interests and refresh your mind after hard work. These hobbies should ideally be useful to you in the future. For example, after you leave the screen, you can turn the hobbies you are familiar with into your profession, such as calligraphy, painting, music, etc.

"When your career gradually shows promise, you must not assume that your position is stable, and you must not indulge in pleasure. You should work as hard as you did when you first arrived in Hollywood. You must always remember that the success and rewards you have achieved are temporary and fleeting. Don't spend all your income. You should save part of it as a precaution for the future. If your weekly income is twenty-five dollars, you should save five dollars. Although this amount is not large, it can help you develop a habit of thrift and constantly generate a warning force in your mind, so that you will not forget to continue to work hard."

What Mary Pickford said above is, of course, for young American women who want to enter the film industry. But the words contained therein are all truths. All our young men and women who want to enter the film industry should also read them carefully, so that they can also know some of the necessary conditions for entering the film industry and the mistakes that should be avoided. (The End)

Movie Reviews

Review of "One Hour Late"

— Ling He

One Hour Late — Da Guangming —

As a comedy, "One Hour Late" constructs a relatively complex story in twelve hours, which at least makes people feel that the progress of the play is quite compact. This fully demonstrates the modernity of American movies, the fast tempo, the bright tone, the laughter, the superficial, the light and lively, so that the audience accepts the entertainment given to them by the author.

The beginning is so bright: the children's quarrelsome crying, the heroine can not sleep peacefully, the pain of the unemployed disappears in the laughter. This is at 6:30 in the morning. Then the heroine arrives at the electrical company. From the entanglement of love between the hero and heroine, to the heroine's flattered seduction by the manager, plus the atmosphere of the office, all fully express the sincerity of the petit bourgeois writer's sketch of the city, and these become the most brilliant performance of this film. All the way down to the office, almost to 6:30 in the afternoon, the elevator breaks down, making the plot suddenly tense. But neither the playwright nor the director succeeded here. The hero's singing completely destroys the tense atmosphere. If it is said that it is to gain the appreciation of the radio station owner, then there are plenty of opportunities to write it in other scenes, and there is no need to destroy the atmosphere here. The happy ending that followed was even more mediocre.

Judging from the ending, the playwright ultimately did not have her combine with the manager, which seems to be a more desirable place, and writing about the manager's collusion with female employees, in contrast to writing about the manager's wife and lover messing around, naturally has an expository meaning, but in the end, the manager and his wife end up as good as ever, so that what was written before becomes completely wasted. As for the heroine's immediate awakening because of the hero's bravery, regardless of whether the beauty really likes brave men so much, it always makes people feel forced. Such rashness is not an attitude that an artist should have. In this place, the vulgarity of the author is expressed.

Helen Twelvetrees' acting skills are very satisfying. She can act. And just right, in the first part completely expresses what the director wants to express. The male lead and the others all perform their duties mediocrely.

Review of "Gift Gab"

— You Jing

Gift Gab — Great Shanghai Screening —

I remember when sound films first emerged, "So-and-so Convention" and "So-and-so Gala Performance," these types of films featuring the entire cast of a company, so-called All Stars, were once extremely popular. Later, due to the regular application of sound technology, they progressed from chaotic patchwork to sound films with content and structure. However, things have changed, and All-Star films have been revived due to objective reasons.

The so-called objective reason is not that the audience needs this type of film again, but the motives for making these All-Star films before and after are absolutely not the same. The former was based on the limitations of sound film technology, and it was necessary to gather some singing and dancing scenes to cater to the general enthusiasm of the audience for sound films; the latter, however, is when the market is sluggish and business is depressed, they have to use All-Stars with cheap stars to attract the audience.

In order to allow every star who appears to have a role to play, and there is no story of that kind that meets this requirement, so this latter type of All-Star film, made under different conditions, naturally relapses into the old pattern of the former type in essence—no complete story, no sound script with a tight structure, just a piecemeal mix like a bowl of "mixed vegetables."

This "Gift Gab" is that kind of "mixed vegetables". The simple and clichéd story is about a brilliant student named Gabner who joins a radio broadcasting station as an announcer for broadcasting programs. He becomes famous because of the admiration of Miss Babola, a colleague. He loses his job because of being obsessed with a love triangle and falsely reporting news. Then, through a daring act, he restores his reputation, status, and love with a woman, ending in a happy reunion. —It’s very lively to call all the All Stars to appear.

Here, we don’t treat the so-called Valne of All Stars in "Gift Gab" as we should, we only need to see how the producers handle this All Star to know whether the film is successful or not. They painstakingly used the radio station as a magical treasure—a telescopic ring, incorporating a large number of stars in a comprehensive way, lengthening the picture, broadcasting famous songs, music teams, singing groups, and thrilling dramas co-starred by big stars, continuing without principles or tailoring. Perhaps the smart producers also felt the embarrassment of continuing like this? So they unscrupulously reused the familiar and tired-of-seeing sports competitions and jumps from airplanes. As for the lengthy and repetitive reports before the Radio, the vulgar and old-fashioned Happy Ending suffering the cold gaze of the audience, are even smaller things!

Naturally, there are also many successful aspects here, such as some of the humor in the dialogue and actions, the clown making funny faces, and the complex male and female relationships, all of which successfully won the laughter of the audience, although this cannot be said to be the success of the entire film.

Director Karl Frnnp managed to be busy for a while handling so many people and the things they were pulling. As for the lack of grasp of the dramatic atmosphere, it was determined by the script.

Among the big gatherings of thirty stars, no one competed to show off their skills. In terms of acting skills, Edmund Lowe, Rose Ading, and Phil Batur were only trying their best, and the rest were even more "not very good".

"Winning Back Her Husband" scene, the one in equestrian polo costume is Oly England, in the middle is Reynaldo Deni, and on the right is Manjani Nickson—Nanjing Screening

Movie Novel

National Sound (Bordertown) (6)

— Xue Mei

The invitations have been sent out, and La Ruda—"Monte Carlo in the Desert"—will soon open... The meal fee is twenty-five yuan per person. That was Johnny's trick... Intended to attract upper class people—the aristocracy of society, and give them a good knock. Sure enough, the general upper class people arrived as scheduled. They came to this "Monte Carlo in the Desert" in groups, and were warmly entertained by the host Johnny Ramirez. He was wearing a tuxedo and dressed neatly. At this time, all the chaotic sounds of the silver shoes subsided. But in La Ruda, there was a Spanish atmosphere. Although the large restaurant was crowded with people, it still felt spacious. There were gambling tables upstairs and downstairs, but they were all located in secret places. And there was also a small band playing exquisite music.

The business of La Ruda on opening day was so good that it could not be better. Guests who arrived late without reserving a seat had almost no room to stand. They all had to ask the host Johnny Ramirez to make special arrangements. Mr. Jiang had to refuse politely. But once, he made a special accommodation. That was for a lady. She was not a regular customer there, but he knew her. He saw her standing at the entrance, and his heart couldn't help but thump. He also knew the companion she was with, who was a noble colleague who caused him to stop his law career.

When Dale Elwell saw him, she couldn't help but smile and said, "Really, are you the owner of this place?" Johnny smiled and replied, "Believe it or not." Her male companion interjected, "We have to find a table to sit down." Dale put her slender hand in Johnny's arm and smiled, "Come on, barbarian." Johnny said, "Barbarian? Do you think I don't know how to serve women and move chairs for them?" Dale said, "Don't rush. Let's try it out first." She had no affectation of arrogance. She and him seemed to be old acquaintances.

They sat together, they danced together. Finally, they sat together in the conservatory, a long window facing the desert outside. At this time, the bright moon hung high in the sky, shining on a flat and boundless sandy plain, which was very imposing. Dale couldn't help but admire, "It's really unbelievable that you were able to create such a situation in such a short period of time. I think your wife must be very happy." Johnny laughed, "I haven't married yet, so where would I get a wife?" Dale said strangely, "What? A handsome young man with a great career hasn't been caught yet?"

Dale was teasing him like this. He was a courageous man, but he was a clumsy man with no experience with the opposite sex. At this time, he couldn't help but stammer, "I—I—haven't talked about this before. You made me speechless for a moment." Dale said, "No way. You wouldn't be speechless. Your only fault is that you don't know how to pretend. Do you want me to teach you? Okay. Don't be too serious. Tonight is a night of love. It should be romantic, my good boy." As she said, she hooked her hand on Johnny's arm, leaned her head on his shoulder, and then asked, "Are you comfortable?" Johnny said, "No." Dale said, "I'll tell you a secret, I also feel a little uncomfortable, my heart is thumping."

Johnny was teased by her, and he was about to kiss her when Dale suddenly sat up straight and said, "Someone is coming." Johnny looked up and saw that it was none other than Mary Luke standing in front of them. She said, "I'm sorry to interrupt your conversation." Johnny got up angrily, grabbed Mary's arm and said, "Come here." He led her to his office and asked her, "What do you think you're doing? Running to this place to spy on my actions? Why did you interrupt when I was talking to someone else?" Mary laughed wildly for a while, and then her body and appearance gradually changed. Although she had grown fat, her face was still very haggard. Her eyes seemed to not see things accurately. (To be continued)
